\hat{I}_i = \sum_{e_2 = 1}^{n_{e1}^2}\sum_{j,j = 1}^{n_{e2}^e}\left[u_{l_2(e_2,jj)}d_{ii,jj,n_e}(e_2) + w_{l_2(e,jj)}d_{ii,jj,n_e}(e_2)\right]. \tag{17.13}
\end{equation}

\section{System Jacobian}
The system of equations given by the Residuals has the following Jacobian
\begin{equation}
JR =
\begin{bmatrix}
\partial_u \hat{M}^r & \partial_w \hat{M}^r & \partial_p \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{M}^r & \partial_h \hat{M}^r \\
\partial_u \hat{M}^z & \partial_w \hat{M}^z & \partial_p \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{M}^z & \partial_h \hat{M}^z \\
\partial_u \hat{C}   & \partial_w \hat{C}   & \partial_p \hat{C}   & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{C}   & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{C}   & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{C}   & \partial_h \hat{C}   \\
\partial_u \hat{K}   & \partial_w \hat{K}   & \partial_p \hat{K}   & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{K}   & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{K}   & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{K}   & \partial_h \hat{K}   \\
\partial_u \hat{I}   & \partial_w \hat{I}   & \partial_p \hat{I}   & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{I}   & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{I}   & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{I}   & \partial_h \hat{I}   
\end{bmatrix}. \tag{18.1}
\end{equation}
Every entry in the Jacobian matrix can be calculated analytically, with the only exception of the elements on the first column on each block of the last block-column. These elements are calculated quasi-analytically, since the derivatives of the nodal positions with respect to the focal length is approximated numerically.

\subsection{Entries on the first block-row}
Blocks in the first row are given by
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_u \hat{M}^r\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ q=l(e,kk)}} \left\{ Re \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^v} u_{l(e,jj)} a_{ii,kk,jj}^r(e) + \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^v} \left[ Re A_{ii,jj}(u,w,e) + 2a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) + a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) \right] \right\} \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ q=l_2(e_2,jj)}} Be \, d_{t_r,t_r,ii,jj}(e_2), \tag{18.2}\\
\left(\partial_w \hat{M}^r\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ q=l(e,kk)}} Re u_{l(e,jj)} a_{ii,kk,jj}^z(e) + \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{q=l(e,jj)} a_{ii,jj}^{z,r}(e) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ q=l_2(e_2,jj)}} Be \, d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2), \tag{18.3}\\
\left(\partial_p \hat{M}^r\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ q=l_p(e,jj)}} b_{jj,ii}^r(e), \tag{18.4}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^2} \hat{M}^r\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}^2} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2), \tag{18.5}
\end{align}
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_h \hat{M}^r\right)_{i,q} &= 
\sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S(e,qq)}}^{n_e^v} \Bigg( u_{l(e,jj)} \Bigg[ Re \sum_{kk=1}^{n_e^v} \big( u_{l(e,kk)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,kk,jj}^r(e) + w_{l(e,kk)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,kk,jj}^z(e) \big) \nonumber\\
&\qquad + 2 \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) + \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) \Bigg] + w_{l(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{z,r}(e) \Bigg) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S(e,qq)}}^{n_e^p} p_{l_p(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} b_{jj,ii}^r(e) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_1=1}^{n_{el}^1} \sum_{\substack{i=l_1(e_1,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_1(e_1,qq)}}^{n_e^v} \frac{1}{Ca} \omega_{l_1^1(e_1,jj)}^1 \partial_{h_{S_1(e_1,qq)}} c_{t_r,jj,ii}^s(e_1) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}} Be \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_r,t_r,ii}(e_2) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}}^{n_{e_2}^{2,v}} Be \Big( u_{l_2(e_2,jj)} \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_r,t_r,ii,jj}(e_2) + w_{l_2(e_2,jj)} \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2) \Big) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ j=1\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}}^{n_{e_2}^v} \varpi_{l_2^2(e_2,jj)}^2 \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_3=1}^{n_{el}^3} \sum_{\substack{i=l_3(e_3,ii)\\ j=1\\ q=S_3(e_3,qq)}}^{n_{e_3}^v} \Big( \varpi_{l_3^3(e_3,jj)}^3 \partial_{h_{S_3(e_3,qq)}} f_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_3) + \varrho_{l_3^3(e_3,jj)}^3 \partial_{h_{S_3(e_3,qq)}} f_{t_r,ii,jj}(e_3) \Big). \tag{18.8}
\end{align}

\subsection{Entries on the second block-row}
Blocks in the second row are given by
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_u \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}} \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^e} Re w_{l(e,jj)} a_{ii,kk,jj}^r(e) + \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}} a_{ii,jj}^r(e) + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{e1}^2} Be d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj}, \tag{18.9}\\
\left(\partial_w \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}} \left\{ \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^e} \left[ Re A_{ii,jj}(u,w,e) + 2a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) + a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) \right] \right. \nonumber\\
&\qquad \left. + \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^e} Re w_{l(e,jj)} a_{ii,kk,jj}^r(e) \right\} + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_e^2} Be d_{t_z,t_z,ii,jj}, \tag{18.10}\\
\left(\partial_p \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}} -b_{jj,ii}^z(e), \tag{18.11}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^2} \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}^2} d_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_2), \tag{18.12}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^3} \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}^3} f_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_3), \tag{18.13}\\
\left(\partial_{\gamma^3} \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{e1}^3} f_{ii,jj}(e_3), \tag{18.14}
\end{align}
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_h \hat{M}^z\right)_{i,q} &= 
\sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S(e,qq)}}^{n_e^v} \Bigg( w_{l(e,jj)} \Bigg[ Re \sum_{kk=1}^{n_e^v} \big( u_{l(e,kk)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,kk,jj}^r(e) + w_{l(e,kk)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,kk,jj}^z(e) \big) \nonumber\\
&\qquad + 2 \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) + \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) \Bigg] + u_{l(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii,jj}^{r,z}(e) \Bigg) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ q=S(e,qq)}} St \, \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} a_{ii}(e) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{\substack{i=l(e,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S(e,qq)}}^{n_e^p} p_{l_p(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} b_{jj,ii}^z(e) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_1=1}^{n_{el}^1} \sum_{\substack{i=l_1(e_1,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_1(e_1,qq)}}^{n_{e1}^v} \frac{1}{Ca} \omega_{l_1^1(e_1,jj)}^1 \partial_{h_{S_1(e_1,qq)}} c_{t_z,jj,ii}^s(e_1) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}} Be \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_r,t_z,ii} \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}}^{n_{e_2}^{2,v}} Be \Big( u_{l_2(e_2,jj)} \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj} + w_{l_2(e_2,jj)} \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{t_z,t_z,ii,jj} \Big) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_2=1}^{n_{el}^2} \sum_{\substack{i=l_2(e_2,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}}^{n_{e_2}^v} \varpi_{l_2^2(e_2,jj)}^2 \partial_{h_{S_2(e_2,qq)}} d_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_2) \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{e_3=1}^{n_{el}^3} \sum_{\substack{i=l_3(e_3,ii)\\ jj=1\\ q=S_3(e_3,qq)}}^{n_{e_3}^{3,v}} \Big( \varpi_{l_3^3(e_3,jj)}^3 \partial_{h_{S_3(e_3,qq)}} f_{ii,jj,n_z} + \varrho_{l_3(e_3,jj)}^3 \partial_{h_{S_3(e_3,qq)}} f_{t_z,ii,jj}(e_3) \Big). \tag{18.15}
\end{align}

\subsection{Entries on the third block-row}
Blocks in the third row are given by
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_u \hat{C}\right)_{k,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} b_{jj,ii}^p(e), \tag{18.16}\\
\left(\partial_w \hat{C}\right)_{k,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} b_{jj,ii}^z(e), \tag{18.17}\\
\left(\partial_p \hat{C}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.18}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^2} \hat{C}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.19}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^3} \hat{C}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.20}\\
\left(\partial_h \hat{C}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e=1}^{n_{el}} \sum_{jj=1}^{n_e^e} \left[ u_{l(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} b_{ii,jj}^p(e) + w_{l(e,jj)} \partial_{h_{S(e,qq)}} b_{ii,jj}^z(e) \right]. \tag{18.22}
\end{align}

\subsection{Entries on the fourth block-row}
Blocks in the fourth row are given by
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_u \hat{K}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e_1=1}^{n_{e1}^1} c_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_1), \tag{18.23}\\
\left(\partial_w \hat{K}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{e_1=1}^{n_{e1}^1} c_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_1), \tag{18.24}\\
\left(\partial_p \hat{K}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.25}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^2} \hat{K}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.26}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^3} \hat{K}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.27}
\end{align}

\subsection{Entries on the fifth block-row}
Blocks in the fifth row are given by
\begin{align}
\left(\partial_u \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{\substack{i=l_2^2(e_2,ii)\\ q=l_2(e_2,jj)}} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2), \tag{18.30}\\
\left(\partial_w \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{\substack{i=l_2^2(e_2,ii)\\ q=l_2(e_2,jj)}} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2), \tag{18.31}\\
\left(\partial_p \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.32}\\
\left(\partial_{\lambda^2} \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.33}\\
\left(\partial_{\nu^3} \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.34}\\
\left(\partial_s \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{18.35}\\
\left(\partial_h \hat{I}\right)_{i,q} &= \sum_{\substack{i=l_2^2(e,ii)\\ q=S_2(e_2,qq)}} \left[ u_{l_2(e_2,jj)} \partial_{h_q} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2) + w_{l_2(e,jj)} \partial_{h_q} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_\ell) \right]. \tag{18.36}
\end{align}

\subsection{Jacobian with explicit zero-blocks}
Re-writing the Jacobian indicating null blocks we have
\begin{equation}
JR =
\begin{bmatrix}
\partial_u \hat{M}^r & \partial_w \hat{M}^r & \partial_p \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{M}^r & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{M}^r & \partial_h \hat{M}^r \\
\partial_u \hat{M}^z & \partial_w \hat{M}^z & \partial_p \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\omega^2} \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{M}^z & \partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{M}^z & \partial_h \hat{M}^z \\
\partial_u \hat{C}   & \partial_w \hat{C}   & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & \partial_h \hat{C}   \\
\partial_u \hat{K}   & \partial_w \hat{K}   & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & \partial_h \hat{K}   \\
\partial_u \hat{I}   & \partial_w \hat{I}   & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & \partial_h \hat{I}   
\end{bmatrix}. \tag{18.37}
\end{equation}
We highlight that when boundary 2 is a straight line parallel to the \(r\) axis, we also have
\begin{equation}
\partial_{\omega^2} \hat{M}^r = 0, \tag{18.38}
\end{equation}
and when boundary 3 is a straight line parallel to the \(z\) axis, we also have
\begin{equation}
\partial_{\epsilon^3} \hat{M}^r = 0, \qquad \partial_{\omega^3} \hat{M}^z = 0. \tag{18.39-40}
\end{equation}

\section{Basis functions}
We follow Sprittles \& Shikhmurzaev (2012b) and use the V6P3 Taylor-Hood master element, see figure 10 to which we map every element in our domain isoparametrically (see below for details).

Pressure interpolating functions \(\psi\) are given by:
\begin{align}
\psi_{1} &= \frac{1 + \eta}{2}, \tag{19.1}\\
\psi_{2} &= -\frac{\xi + \eta}{2}, \tag{19.2}\\
\psi_{3} &= \frac{1 + \xi}{2}. \tag{19.3}
\end{align}
Nodes 1, 2 and 3 are pressure-velocity nodes, while 4, 5 and 6 are velocity only nodes. The sub-index in functions \(\psi\) indicate on which of the pressure-velocity nodes the functions attain the value 1, being zero in the other two, and linear over each element.

Velocity interpolating functions \(\phi\) are defined as follows
\begin{align}
\phi_{1} &= \psi_{1}(2\psi_{1} - 1) = \frac{1 + \eta}{2} (1 + \eta - 1) = \frac{\eta(\eta + 1)}{2} = \frac{\eta^{2} + \eta}{2}, \tag{19.4}\\
\phi_{2} &= \psi_{2}(2\psi_{2} - 1) = -\frac{\xi + \eta}{2} (-\xi -\eta - 1) = \frac{(\xi + \eta)(\xi + \eta + 1)}{2} = \frac{\xi^{2} + \eta^{2} + 2\xi\eta + \xi + \eta}{2}, \tag{19.5}\\
\phi_{3} &= \psi_{3}(2\psi_{3} - 1) = \frac{1 + \xi}{2} (1 + \xi - 1) = \frac{\xi(\xi + 1)}{2} = \frac{\xi^{2} + \xi}{2}, \tag{19.6}\\
\phi_{4} &= 4\psi_{1}\psi_{3} = 4\frac{1 + \eta}{2}\frac{1 + \xi}{2} = (\xi + 1)(\eta + 1) = \xi\eta +\xi +\eta +1, \tag{19.7}\\
\phi_{5} &= 4\psi_{2}\psi_{1} = -4\frac{\xi + \eta}{2}\frac{1 + \eta}{2} = -(\xi +\eta)(\eta + 1) = -\eta^{2} - \xi\eta -\xi -\eta , \tag{19.8}\\
\phi_{6} &= 4\psi_{3}\psi_{2} = -4\frac{1 + \xi}{2}\frac{\xi + \eta}{2} = -(\xi +\eta)(\xi + 1) = -\xi^{2} - \xi\eta -\xi -\eta . \tag{19.9}
\end{align}
Function \(S_{e}(\xi,\eta)\) maps the coordinates of the master element to the coordinates of element number \(e\). More specifically
\begin{equation}
(r^{e},z^{e}) = S_{e}(\xi,\eta). \tag{19.10}
\end{equation}
The fact that our mapping is isoparametric means that, much like the pressure and velocity functions, the \(r_e\) and \(z_e\) coordinates of the points in a given element are described as
\begin{equation}
r_e = \sum_{jj = 1}^{6} r_{e,jj} \phi_{jj}, \tag{19.11}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
z_e = \sum_{jj = 1}^{6} z_{e,jj} \phi_{jj}, \tag{19.12}
\end{equation}
with \(r_{e,jj}\) being the \(r\) coordinate of local node \(jj\) in element \(e\). The obvious analogy applies to \(z\).

\subsection{Derivatives of the basis functions}
The derivatives of the velocity interpolating functions with respect to \(\xi\) are given by:
\begin{align}
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{1} &= 0, \tag{19.13}\\
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{2} &= \xi +\eta +\frac{1}{2}, \tag{19.14}\\
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{3} &= \xi +\frac{1}{2}, \tag{19.15}\\
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{4} &= \eta +1, \tag{19.16}\\
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{5} &= -\eta -1, \tag{19.17}\\
\partial_{\xi}\phi_{6} &= -2\xi -\eta -1. \tag{19.18}
\end{align}
The derivatives of the velocity interpolating functions with respect to \(\eta\) are given by:
\begin{align}
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{1} &= \eta +\frac{1}{2}, \tag{19.19}\\
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{2} &= \xi +\eta +\frac{1}{2}, \tag{19.20}\\
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{3} &= 0, \tag{19.21}\\
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{4} &= \xi +1, \tag{19.22}\\
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{5} &= -2\eta -\xi -1, \tag{19.23}\\
\partial_{\eta}\phi_{6} &= -\xi -1. \tag{19.24}
\end{align}

\section{Integrals over triangular elements}
In order to simplify our calculations, it is convenient to express all integrals over an element as integrals over the master element. This requires changing the \(r\) and \(z\) variables of the element coordinates to the \(\xi\) and \(\eta\) variables of the master element. That is to say, we need to consider
\begin{equation}
\int_{\Omega_e} f(r,z) \, dr\,dz = \int_{\eta=-1}^{1} \int_{\xi=-1}^{1} f(\xi,\eta) \, |\det J_e| \, d\xi\, d\eta, \tag{20.1}
\end{equation}
where \(J_e\) is the Jacobian of the isoparametric map \(S_e\) for that element, given by
\begin{equation}
J_e = \begin{bmatrix}
\frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \xi} & \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \eta} \\[4pt]
\frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \xi} & \frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \eta}
\end{bmatrix}, \tag{20.2}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\det J_e = \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \eta} - \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \eta} \frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \xi}. \tag{20.3}
\end{equation}
From (19.11) and (19.12) we have
\begin{equation}
\det J_e = \left(\sum_{i=1}^6 r_{e,i} \frac{\partial \phi_i}{\partial \xi}\right) \left(\sum_{j=1}^6 z_{e,j} \frac{\partial \phi_j}{\partial \eta}\right) - \left(\sum_{i=1}^6 r_{e,i} \frac{\partial \phi_i}{\partial \eta}\right) \left(\sum_{j=1}^6 z_{e,j} \frac{\partial \phi_j}{\partial \xi}\right), \tag{20.4}
\end{equation}
i.e.
\begin{equation}
\det J_e = \sum_{i=1}^6 \sum_{j=1}^6 r_{e,i} \left( \frac{\partial \phi_i}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial \phi_j}{\partial \eta} - \frac{\partial \phi_j}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial \phi_i}{\partial \eta} \right) z_{e,j}. \tag{20.6}
\end{equation}
Furthermore, if we make sure that the local numbering in all our elements is done in the same direction as our master element (counter-clockwise), and we do not have degenerate elements, we can ensure that the determinant of the Jacobian is always positive (which we assume from here on).

Many of the integrals over elements that are needed to create our system of equations and its Jacobian require that we calculate derivatives of the interpolating functions with respect to \(r\) and \(z\). Following Sprattles \& Shikhmurzaev (2012b), we will calculate these using the chain rule, first taking derivatives with respect to \(\xi\) and \(\eta\) and then differentiating \(\xi\) and \(\eta\) with respect to \(r_e\) and \(z_e\). We do this by noticing that
\begin{equation}
J_e^{-1} = \begin{bmatrix}
\frac{\partial \xi}{\partial r_e} & \frac{\partial \xi}{\partial z_e} \\[4pt]
\frac{\partial \eta}{\partial r_e} & \frac{\partial \eta}{\partial z_e}
\end{bmatrix} = \frac{1}{\det J_e} \begin{bmatrix}
\frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \eta} & -\frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \eta} \\[4pt]
-\frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \xi} & \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \xi}
\end{bmatrix}, \tag{20.7}
\end{equation}
where the left equality follows by definition and the right one is the computation of the inverse from the expression in (20.2). We thus have
\begin{align}
\frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial r_e} &= \frac{1}{\det J_e} \left( \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \eta} - \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \eta} \frac{\partial z_e}{\partial \xi} \right) \nonumber\\
&= \frac{1}{\det J_e} \left[ \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \xi} \left( \sum_{kk} z_{e,kk} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \eta} \right) - \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \eta} \left( \sum_{kk} z_{e,kk} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \xi} \right) \right] \nonumber\\
&= \frac{1}{\det J_e} \sum_{kk=1}^6 \left( \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \eta} - \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \eta} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \xi} \right) z_{e,kk}, \tag{20.11}
\end{align}
and similarly
\begin{align}
\frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial z_e} &= \frac{1}{\det J_e} \left( -\frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \eta} + \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \eta} \frac{\partial r_e}{\partial \xi} \right) \nonumber\\
&= \frac{1}{\det J_e} \sum_{kk=1}^6 \left( -\frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \xi} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \eta} + \frac{\partial \phi_{jj}}{\partial \eta} \frac{\partial \phi_{kk}}{\partial \xi} \right) r_{e,kk}. \tag{20.15}
\end{align}
Hence, we have now all the elements needed to compute all integrals over elements using the map to the master element.

\subsection{Integrals over elements mapped to master element}
Integration over the master element will be carried out using Gaussian quadrature, following Zhang et al. (2009). Therefore, all integrals will be transformed into sums over sampling points. Here we give the expression for each integral over a triangular element that was used above. Boxed equations correspond to the most convenient way of expressing the terms when coding them.

\subsubsection{a terms}
From (??), we have
\begin{align}
a_{g_r,ii}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} g_r \phi_{l(e,ii)} \tag{20.16}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) g_r \phi_{ii}(p) \det J_e(p). \tag{20.18}\\
a_{ii,jj}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \phi_{l(e,ii)} \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.19}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p) \det J_e(p). \tag{20.21}\\
a_{ii,kk,jj}^{r}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \phi_{l(e,ii)} \phi_{l(e,kk)} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.22}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{kk}(p) \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{jj,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right), \tag{20.25}\\
a_{ii,kk,jj}^{z}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \phi_{l(e,ii)} \phi_{l(e,kk)} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.26}\\
&\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{kk}(p) \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{jj,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right), \tag{20.28}\\
a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,ii)} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.29}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn=1}^6 T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) }, \tag{20.31}\\
a_{ii,jj}^{z,r}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,ii)} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.32}\\
&\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn=1}^6 T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) }, \tag{20.34}\\
a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,ii)} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.35}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn=1}^6 T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) }, \tag{20.37}\\
a_{ii,jj}^{r,z}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,ii)} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,jj)} \tag{20.38}\\
&\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn=1}^6 T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) }, \tag{20.40}\\
a_{g_z,ii}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} g_z \phi_{l(e,ii)} \tag{20.41}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) g_z \phi_{ii}(p) \det J_e(p). \tag{20.43}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{b terms}
From equation (??) we have
\begin{align}
b_{jj,ii}^{r}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \psi_{l_p(e,jj)} \partial_r \phi_{l(e,ii)} \tag{20.44}\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \psi_{jj}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm}, \tag{20.47}\\
b_{jj,ii}^{z}(e) &= \int_{\Omega_e} \psi_{l_p(e,jj)} \partial_z \phi_{l(e,ii)} \tag{20.48}\\
&\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \psi_{jj}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm}. \tag{20.50}
\end{align}

\subsection{Derivatives of integrals over triangle elements}
The expressions above contain all terms that depend on the coordinates of each element. In order to calculate the derivatives of the residuals with respect to the lengths of the spines, we need to calculate the derivatives of these expressions. In the above expressions, all functions are independent of the location of the nodes, except for \(r_{e,mm}\), \(z_{e,mm}\) and \(\det J_e\). We consider now the derivative of \(\det J_e\)
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} \det J_e &= \sum_{i=1}^6 \sum_{j=1}^6 \left[ (\partial_{h_q} r_{e,i}) T_{ii,jj} z_{e,j} + r_{e,i} T_{ii,jj} (\partial_{h_q} z_{e,j}) \right]. \tag{20.52}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{Derivatives of a terms}
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} a_{g_r,ii}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) g_r \phi_{ii}(p) \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.55}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,jj}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p) \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.58}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,kk,jj}^{r}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{kk}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{jj,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,mm}, \tag{20.61}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,kk,jj}^{z}(e) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{kk}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{jj,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,mm}, \tag{20.64}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,jj}^{r,r}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ [\det J_e(p)]^2 } \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.67}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,jj}^{r,z}(e) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) z_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ [\det J_e(p)]^2 } \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.70}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,jj}^{z,r}(e) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) z_{e,nn} \right) }{ [\det J_e(p)]^2 } \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.73}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{ii,jj}^{z,z}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,nn} \right) }{ \det J_e(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \frac{ \left( \sum_{mm} T_{ii,mm}(p) r_{e,mm} \right) \left( \sum_{nn} T_{jj,nn}(p) r_{e,nn} \right) }{ [\det J_e(p)]^2 } \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p), \tag{20.76}\\
\partial_{h_q} a_{g_z,ii}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) g_z \phi_{ii}(p) \partial_{h_q} \det J_e(p). \tag{20.79}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{Derivatives of b terms}
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} b_{jj,ii}^{r}(e) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \psi_{jj}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} z_{e,mm}, \tag{20.82}\\
\partial_{h_q} b_{jj,ii}^{z}(e) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_G} W(p) \psi_{jj}(p) \sum_{mm=1}^6 T_{ii,mm}(p) \partial_{h_q} r_{e,mm}. \tag{20.85}
\end{align}

\section{Integrals over line elements}
\subsection{The free-surface line elements}
From (??) we have
\begin{equation}
c_{t_r,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) = \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_1}} t_r^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,jj)}^1 \partial_s \phi_{i_1(e_1,ii)}^1. \tag{21.1}
\end{equation}
In order to simplify our calculations when we consider the integral above and others on the same boundary, we will ensure that our line elements that lay on the free-surface always correspond to the side of the element containing the nodes of local number 2, 6 and 3 (see figure 10). Hence, line-elements on boundary 1 are easily parameterised by the variable \(\xi\). More specifically we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^1(\xi) &= \phi_2(\xi,\eta=-1), \tag{21.2}\\
\phi_2^1(\xi) &= \phi_6(\xi,\eta=-1), \tag{21.3}\\
\phi_3^1(\xi) &= \phi_3(\xi,\eta=-1), \tag{21.4}
\end{align}
since the line element is given by the equation \(\eta=-1\) in the master element.
From equation (19.5) we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^1(\xi) &= \frac{\xi^2 - \xi}{2}, \tag{21.6}\\
\phi_2^1(\xi) &= -\xi^2 + 1, \tag{21.8}\\
\phi_3^1(\xi) &= \frac{\xi^2 + \xi}{2}, \tag{21.9}
\end{align}
and consequently
\begin{align}
\partial_\xi \phi_1^1(\xi) &= \xi - \frac12, \tag{21.10}\\
\partial_\xi \phi_2^1(\xi) &= -2\xi, \tag{21.11}\\
\partial_\xi \phi_3^1(\xi) &= \xi + \frac12. \tag{21.12}
\end{align}
We can calculate the tangent to the line element by
\begin{equation}
t^1 = \frac{ (\partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1, \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1) }{ \sqrt{ (\partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1)^2 + (\partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1)^2 } }, \tag{21.13}
\end{equation}
where the tangent points in the direction of increasing \(\xi\) and \(r_{e_1}^1\) is the \(r\) coordinate along on element \(e_1\) on boundary 1. \(r_{e_1}^1\) and its analogue for \(z\) are defined by the map \(S_{e_1}^1\) which takes the interval \([-1,1]\) to the line element in boundary one, i.e.
\begin{equation}
(r_{e_1}^1, z_{e_1}^1) = S_{e_1}^1(\xi). \tag{21.14}
\end{equation}
Moreover, we have
\begin{align}
\partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1 &= \sum_{jj=1}^3 r_{e_1,jj}^1 \partial_\xi \phi_{jj}^1, \tag{21.15}\\
\partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1 &= \sum_{jj=1}^3 z_{e_1,jj}^1 \partial_\xi \phi_{jj}^1, \tag{21.16}
\end{align}
and we introduce
\begin{equation}
J_{e_1}^1 \coloneqq \partial_\xi s = \sqrt{ (\partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1)^2 + (\partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1)^2 }, \tag{21.19}
\end{equation}
which is the determinant of the Jacobian of \(S_{e_1}^1\). The integral (21.1) can be rewritten as
\begin{equation}
c_{t_r,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) = \int_{\xi=-1}^{1} \frac{ \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(\xi) }{ J_{e_1}^1(\xi) } \phi_{jj}^1(\xi) \partial_s \phi_{ii}^1(\xi) \, \partial_\xi s = \int_{\xi=-1}^{1} \frac{ \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(\xi) }{ J_{e_1}^1(\xi) } \phi_{jj}^1(\xi) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(\xi) \, d\xi. \tag{21.21}
\end{equation}
Hence, using Gaussian quadrature we have
\begin{equation}
c_{t_r,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) \approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p). \tag{21.22}
\end{equation}
Similarly,
\begin{align}
c_{t_z,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) &= \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_1}} t_z^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,jj)}^1 \partial_s \phi_{i_1(e_1,ii)}^1 \nonumber\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p), \tag{21.25}\\
c_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_1) &= \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_1}} n_r^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,ii)}^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,jj)}^1 \approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) \phi_{ii}^1(p) \phi_{jj}^1(p), \tag{21.29}\\
c_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_1) &= \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_1}} n_z^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,ii)}^1 \phi_{i_1(e_1,jj)}^1 \approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) \phi_{ii}^1(p) \phi_{jj}^1(p). \tag{21.32}
\end{align}

\subsection{The liquid-solid surface line elements}
We can also arrange all local node numbering to guarantee that every side of a triangular element that falls on boundary 2 is the side containing local nodes 1, 5 and 2 (see figure 10). This allows us to have a natural parametrisation of these line elements using variable \(\eta\). More specifically we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^2(\eta) &= \phi_2(\xi=-1,\eta), \tag{21.33}\\
\phi_2^2(\eta) &= \phi_5(\xi=-1,\eta), \tag{21.34}\\
\phi_3^2(\eta) &= \phi_1(\xi=-1,\eta), \tag{21.35}
\end{align}
since the line element is given by the equation \(\xi=-1\) in the master element.
From equation (19.5) we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^2(\eta) &= \frac{\eta^2 - \eta}{2}, \tag{21.37}\\
\phi_2^2(\eta) &= -\eta^2 + 1, \tag{21.39}\\
\phi_3^2(\eta) &= \frac{\eta^2 + \eta}{2}, \tag{21.40}
\end{align}
and consequently
\begin{align}
\partial_\eta \phi_1^2(\eta) &= \eta - \frac12, \tag{21.41}\\
\partial_\eta \phi_2^2(\eta) &= -2\eta, \tag{21.42}\\
\partial_\eta \phi_3^2(\eta) &= \eta + \frac12. \tag{21.43}
\end{align}
Now, from (??) we have
\begin{align}
d_{t_r,t_r,ii,jj}(e_2) &= \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_2}} t_r^2 t_r^2 \phi_{l_2(e_2,ii)}^2 \phi_{l_2(e_2,jj)}^2 \nonumber\\
&\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p), \tag{21.50}\\
d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p)) (\partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p)) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p), \tag{21.53}\\
d_{t_z,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p), \tag{21.56}\\
d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p), \tag{21.60}\\
d_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_2) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} W_l(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p). \tag{21.63}
\end{align}

\subsection{The inflow boundary line elements}
As a consequence of our prior choice of local numbering, the line elements along boundary 3 must correspond to the side of the master element that contains nodes 3, 4 and 1 (see figure 10). We then choose to parameterise these line elements using variable \(\xi\). This implies that we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^3(\xi) &= \phi_1(\xi,\eta=-\xi), \tag{21.64}\\
\phi_2^3(\xi) &= \phi_4(\xi,\eta=-\xi), \tag{21.65}\\
\phi_3^3(\xi) &= \phi_3(\xi,\eta=-\xi), \tag{21.66}
\end{align}
since the line element is given by the equation \(\eta=-\xi\) in the master element.
From equation (19.4) we have
\begin{align}
\phi_1^3(\xi) &= \frac{\xi^2 - \xi}{2}, \tag{21.68}\\
\phi_2^3(\xi) &= -\xi^2 + 1, \tag{21.70}\\
\phi_3^3(\xi) &= \frac{\xi^2 + \xi}{2}, \tag{21.71}
\end{align}
and consequently
\begin{align}
\partial_\xi \phi_1^3(\xi) &= \xi - \frac12, \tag{21.72}\\
\partial_\xi \phi_2^3(\xi) &= -2\xi, \tag{21.73}\\
\partial_\xi \phi_3^3(\xi) &= \xi + \frac12. \tag{21.74}
\end{align}
Now, from equation (??) we have
\begin{align}
f_{t_r,ii,jj}(e_3) &= \int_{\partial\Omega_{e_3}} t_r^3 \phi_{l_3(e_3,ii)}^3 \phi_{l_3(e_3,jj)}^3 \approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \partial_\xi r_{e_3}^3(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p), \tag{21.81}\\
f_{t_z,ii,jj}(e_3) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \partial_\xi z_{e_3}^3(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p), \tag{21.84}\\
f_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_3) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \partial_\xi z_{e_3}^3(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p), \tag{21.88}\\
f_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_3) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \partial_\xi r_{e_3}^3(p) \phi_{ii}(p) \phi_{jj}(p). \tag{21.91}
\end{align}

\subsection{Derivatives of line-element integrals}
We recall
\begin{equation}
J_{e_i}^i(p) = \sqrt{ \left( \partial_{\xi_i} r_{e_i}^i(p) \right)^2 + \left( \partial_{\xi_i} z_{e_i}^i(p) \right)^2 }, \tag{21.92}
\end{equation}
where \(\xi_i = \xi\) for \(i=1,3\) and \(\xi_i = \eta\) for \(i=2\); and we notice that
\begin{equation}
\partial_{h_q} J_{e_i}^i(p) = \frac{ \partial_{\xi_i} r_{e_i}^i(p) \partial_{h_q} \left( \partial_{\xi_i} r_{e_i}^i(p) \right) + \partial_{\xi_i} z_{e_i}^i(p) \partial_{h_q} \left( \partial_{\xi_i} z_{e_i}^i(p) \right) }{ J_{e_i}^i(p) }, \tag{21.94}
\end{equation}
which reduces the problem to finding
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} \left( \partial_{\xi_i} r_{e_i}^i \right) &= \sum_{mm=1}^3 \left( \partial_{\xi_i} \phi_{mm}^i \right) \left( \partial_{h_q} r_{e_i,mm}^i \right), \tag{21.97}\\
\partial_{h_q} \left( \partial_{\xi_i} z_{e_i}^i \right) &= \sum_{mm=1}^3 \left( \partial_{\xi_i} \phi_{mm}^i \right) \left( \partial_{h_q} z_{e_i,mm}^i \right). \tag{21.98}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{Derivatives of c terms}
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} c_{t_r,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_1}^1(p) }{ (J_{e_1}^1(p))^2 }, \tag{21.101}\\
\partial_{h_q} c_{t_z,jj,ii}^{s}(e_1) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_1}^1(p) }{ (J_{e_1}^1(p))^2 }, \tag{21.104}\\
\partial_{h_q} c_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_1) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_\xi z_{e_1}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_1}^1(p) }{ (J_{e_1}^1(p))^2 }, \tag{21.107}\\
\partial_{h_q} c_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_1) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) }{ J_{e_1}^1(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \frac{ \phi_{jj}^1(p) \partial_\xi \phi_{ii}^1(p) \partial_\xi r_{e_1}^1(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_1}^1(p) }{ (J_{e_1}^1(p))^2 }. \tag{21.110}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{Derivatives of d terms}
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} d_{t_r,t_r,ii,jj}(e_2) &\approx 2 \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p))^2 \partial_{h_q} J_{e_2}^2(p) }{ (J_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }, \tag{21.113}\\
\partial_{h_q} d_{t_r,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) + \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p)) (\partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p)) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_2}^2(p) }{ (J_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }, \tag{21.116}\\
\partial_{h_q} d_{t_z,t_z,ii,jj}(e_2) &\approx 2 \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ (\partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p))^2 \partial_{h_q} J_{e_2}^2(p) }{ (J_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }, \tag{21.119}\\
\partial_{h_q} d_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_2) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta z_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_2}^2(p) }{ (J_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }, \tag{21.122}\\
\partial_{h_q} d_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_2) &\approx - \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_{h_q} \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) }{ J_{e_2}^2(p) } \nonumber\\
&\quad + \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^2(p) \phi_{jj}^2(p) \frac{ \partial_\eta r_{e_2}^2(p) \partial_{h_q} J_{e_2}^2(p) }{ (J_{e_2}^2(p))^2 }. \tag{21.125}
\end{align}

\subsubsection{Derivatives of f terms}
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} f_{t_r,ii,jj}(e_3) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^3(p) \phi_{jj}^3(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi r_{e_3}^3(p), \tag{21.128}\\
\partial_{h_q} f_{t_z,ii,jj}(e_3) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^3(p) \phi_{jj}^3(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi z_{e_3}^3(p), \tag{21.131}\\
\partial_{h_q} f_{ii,jj,n_r}(e_3) &\approx \sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^3(p) \phi_{jj}^3(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi z_{e_3}^3(p), \tag{21.134}\\
\partial_{h_q} f_{ii,jj,n_z}(e_3) &\approx -\sum_{p=1}^{n_{IG}} \phi_{ii}^3(p) \phi_{jj}^3(p) \partial_{h_q} \partial_\xi r_{e_3}^3(p). \tag{21.137}
\end{align}

\section{Derivatives of \(r\) and \(z\) with respect to \(h\)}
We will calculate the derivatives of the nodal positions with respect to all spine lengths exactly, and the derivatives of nodal positions with respect to the focal length \(f\) (which we consider to be spine number 1) numerically.

The \(n_q\) nodes placed along spine \(q\) are equally spaced along it, with the first node on the solid surface and the last node on the free surface. The spines are arcs of circumference; except for the first and last ones, which are a horizontal and a vertical segment, respectively. Hence, the \(i\)-th node along a spine, that is not the first or last, is located along the \(q\)-th spine at a fraction \(\alpha_i^q = (i-1)/(n_q-1)\) of its total length, measuring from the solid towards the free surface; and, therefore, its coordinates are
\begin{align}
r_{i,q} &= r_q - R_q \cos\left( \frac{\alpha_i^q h_q}{R_q} \right), \tag{22.1}\\
z_{i,q} &= R_q \sin\left( \frac{\alpha_i^q h_q}{R_q} \right), \tag{22.2}
\end{align}
where \(r_q\) and \(R_q\) are the \(r\) coordinate of the centre, and the radius of the \(q\)-th spine; respectively. Consequently, we have
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} r_{i,q} &= \alpha_i^q \sin\left( \frac{\alpha_i^q h_q}{R_q} \right), \tag{22.3}\\
\partial_{h_q} z_{i,q} &= \alpha_i^q \cos\left( \frac{\alpha_i^q h_q}{R_q} \right). \tag{22.4}
\end{align}
The coordinates of the \(i\)-th node along the last spine are given by
\begin{align}
r_{i,q} &= -f, \tag{22.5}\\
z_{i,q} &= \alpha_i^q h_q, \tag{22.6}
\end{align}
and, therefore, derivatives with respect to the length of the last spine are simply given by
\begin{align}
\partial_{h_q} r_{i,q} &= 0, \tag{22.7}\\
\partial_{h_q} z_{i,q} &= \alpha_i^q. \tag{22.8}
\end{align}
Finally, to calculate derivatives with respect to \(f\) (the focal length, i.e. spine number 1), we perturb the length of \(f\) forward (see figure 11) and backward and we assess the differential quotient given by
\begin{equation}
\partial_f r \approx \frac{r^+ - r^-}{f^+ - f^-}, \tag{22.9}
\end{equation}
where the \(+\) and \(-\) signs indicate the result of the forward and the backward perturbation, respectively. A completely analogous formula applies to the \(z\) coordinate of the nodes.

\end{document}
